### 🔁 RT Jan 19, 2026 · 11:18 PM

In the barber community I follow a company called TPOB. It’s run by a barber who started his own clipper company. He went to China and developed a clipper that’s faster, quieter, and cheaper than the other big clipper companies.

He does everything anonymously, wearing a mask to hide his identity, yet he’s selling a million clippers per year. I mainly watch because it’s just him in all the videos, single-handedly fighting the system and winning.

The benefit I get is educational, but it’s also about giving credit where credit is due. He’s a fine businessman and deserves more respect than he’s been given. He asks his followers what colors they want and what style they want for the next machine, giving people real options.

On top of that, he offers barbers a chance to have a signature clipper by promoting his brand. There are very few things that grab my attention long-term, but this is one of them.

🍻

### 🔁 RT Jan 19, 2026 · 11:19 PM

Look at Reddit. Who actually creates the value and produces the content? Users do.
But who takes the money? The platform does, lol.
Reddit controls the rails (the feed) and then optimizes all of it for ad performance and revenue. Meanwhile, the people spending real time writing posts, answering questions, and building communities get Karma and badges. Most of the time, no meaningful compensation.

And after the IPO, it’s hard not to feel like this got more intense. More monetization pressure, more ad tooling, more “performance” focus while the actual content producers still aren’t sharing in the upside.

I’m not sure how much longer Reddit will keep prevailing, but nothing lasts forever. Their dominance will end someday.

❤️ 10 · 🔁 3 · 👁 350

> When communities genuinely support creators, everyone wins: incentives align toward producing better, more authentic work that builds lasting connections.

### 🔁 RT Jan 20, 2026 · 05:01 AM

Tell me this doesn’t describe what he just posted, but in coin form. Tell me this doesn’t describe what we have done for over a year and what TB is guiding us to but just replace the coin with the community. 

Proof of Work (PoW) cryptocurrencies are digital assets like Bitcoin (BTC), Litecoin (LTC), and Bitcoin Cash (BCH) that use a consensus mechanism requiring miners to expend computational power (solving complex puzzles) to validate transactions and secure the network, earning rewards for adding new blocks. This energy-intensive process ensures decentralized security, preventing fraud by making attacks computationally expensive. 

We’re basically a proof of work community who builds real things, get rewards (receipts) by solving extremely difficult puzzles and then protecting and making it harder to attack our community

### 🔁 RT Jan 22, 2026 · 08:35 AM

I think this is what makes it so hard for newcomers. It’s difficult to know who’s actually educated and safe to learn from. A lot of people sound confident, have large followings, and only months later you realize they weren’t trustworthy, or the constant drama drives you away. There are some great people, that I have learned a lot from along the way. Seems rare to find those. 
It’s an overwhelming time to be new. Newcomers are necessary for growth, yet many are getting pushed out by "shiny words" and BS. Everyone says they want crypto to grow, but that’s hard when it feels like every group is competing to sound smarter or better than the next instead of helping people truly understand and build. Yes, it’s on us to use the resources available and educate ourselves but also like many, I look to people on X to help make sense of this space. Then add in all the scamming, SAD!! 
 
I personally stuck around and learned along the way through the good and bad, for personal reasons. However,I do see why people quit or just never start. 

❗️SADLY i've learned the crypto trenches are no different than the outside trenches. My opinion, in ways..WORSE.

### 🔁 RT Feb 08, 2026 · 03:38 PM

SUNDAY SERVICE

YzY

HOW GOOD AND PLEASANT IT IS  
WHEN BROTHERS AND SISTERS DWELL TOGETHER IN UNITY

Psalm 133

There is a plain goodness in people coming together that no one can quite explain away.

They are not grand people. They rise early or they rise late. They come with the same small troubles riding in their pockets: a child who won't listen, a paycheck that won't stretch, a memory that won't lie quiet. 

Their shoes are scuffed, their coats are thin in places, their hands show the work they do or the work they wish they still had. And yet Sunday after Sunday they find the same door, push it open, and step inside.

They sit down among one another.

Not because everything has been settled, that the hard questions have received neat answers, or because they have suddenly become better than they were last week.

They sit because the other people are there.

And that simple fact begins to do its slow, steady work.

A woman who has cried herself empty during the week looks across the row and sees another woman whose eyes are red too. Nothing is said at first. Then a small nod passes between them, the kind that needs no words, and something in both of them eases a fraction. 

A man who feels he has failed his family hears another man speak plainly about his own failure, not to confess dramatically, just to say it true, and the air changes. The shame that had been choking him loosens its grip by the smallest degree.

They do not preach perfection to one another and pretend the cracks are not there.  

They simply stay near enough for the cracks to touch.

And in that nearness a quiet thing takes place.

One person's small faithfulness feeds another's.

One person's willingness to show up tired and uncertain gives permission to the rest.
 
A hand reaches over and rests on a shaking shoulder.
  
A voice says, low, "I'm glad you're here."  

A bitter cup is passed during the Lord’s Supper, and with it goes the message that you are not invisible.

This is how the change happens.

Not with sudden transformations, but in the patient rubbing of one life against another.

The rough places grow smoother, not because anyone is trying to sand them down, but because people keep brushing up against each other with ordinary kindness.

They forgive clumsily, listen badly sometimes, and then try again.
  
They disappoint and are disappointed and still come back the next Sunday.

And little by little the thing that was hard becomes less hard.  

The heart that had begun to turn to stone remembers how to feel.  

The one who thought he would always carry the weight alone finds the weight divided, not taken away, but shared so it can be borne.

There is no magic in it.  
There is only the stubborn, everyday miracle of people who refuse to let each other disappear.

They are being made better, not by becoming someone else, but by becoming more truly themselves in the presence of the others.  

More patient because someone waited for them.  

More gentle because someone was gentle when they did not deserve it.  

More hopeful because hope was kept alive in the room even when their own had grown low.

So they keep coming, these plain, worn, unfinished people.  

They keep sitting in the same scratched chairs.  

They keep passing what little they have: bread, wine, a quiet word, a long look.

And in their staying, in their nearness, in their plain refusal to scatter,  
something good is being built.  

Something pleasant.  

Something that carries the very breath of God.

They are not yet whole.  
But they are no longer willing to be whole alone.

And that is already a beginning.

AMEN

4NBT

### 💬 Feb 11, 2026 · 05:25 PM

this might be the single most important crate of records in hip-hop history 🤯

‘the college dropout’ contains over a dozen samples with one surprising thing in common: ye dug most of the samples from a single crate of records that was gifted to him by his then-girlfriend’s father.

the crate included records from al green, nina simone, aretha franklin, and more. helping shape the soulful foundation of his 2004 debut. 🔥

what track from the album do you revisit the most?

People are not quite seeing the scale of this. The next Walt Disney of AI is being born right now.
